**66** **Program and Implementation Guide** **Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts**


##### **Family Involvement and Cultural Connections**

The Bluebonnet Learning [TM] K–5 Reading Language Arts Program incorporates letters to families
explaining the unit overview. These letters encourage families to speak about unit themes and ask
students about new learning. Families can bring in background knowledge about the topics and
support the learning of content, vocabulary, and language development. While students explore
culturally rich topics and texts within the units, they can build connections at home with their
families.

##### **Language and Vocabulary Development**


Within the Bluebonnet Learning [TM] K–5 Reading Language Arts Program, there is a continued
emphasis on knowledge coherence and vocabulary development. The supports embedded within
the lessons allow EB students the opportunity to build connections between content and their
home language. The vocabulary sections within the lessons list Spanish cognates that align to the
English vocabulary words. Students can build what they know about the content from one language
to another.


**Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts** **Program and Implementation Guide** **67**


### Assessments

The Bluebonnet Learning [TM] K–5 Reading Language Arts Program assessments allow teachers to
gain critical information about student mastery of standards-based performance tasks. Through
the use of formative assessments embedded in the Grade K–5 lessons, teachers may adjust
instruction as needed to meet the diverse needs of learners. Assessments include the following
formats and are used to gauge student understanding and application of Skills and Knowledge
units.

##### **Daily Formative Assessments**


The daily formative assessments are aligned to each lesson and allow students to demonstrate
learning success on that day’s instruction. These assessments are completed either during
instructional time or as a home-extension and are located in the Activity Book. Formative
assessment strategies include Checks for
Understanding, delivered briefly during
instruction. Checks for Understanding allow
teachers to monitor progress on each primary
focus objective and adjust instruction as needed.
Strategic questioning of students should include
literal, inferential, and evaluative question types.
The use of literal, inferential, and evaluative
questioning allows teachers to examine students
for explicit and inferred information from texts
along with analytical application of skills.

##### **Mid-Unit Assessments**


The mid-unit assessments are embedded within some units to support teachers in progress
monitoring over the course of the unit and tailoring the remaining instructional time as needed.
These mid-unit assessments are accompanied by instructional materials, teacher implementation
directions, and supports for analyzing student performance. Additional Pausing Point days within


**68** **Program and Implementation Guide** **Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts**


the units give teachers the opportunity to reteach or provide additional instructional support in
small groups or 1:1 following the performance analysis.


**Unit Assessments**
Unit assessments offer summative assessment of students’ comprehension of the Knowledge
units. These assessments, which typically take one instructional period, include support for
analysis of errors and assessment charts to record student progress. These assessments are


**Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts** **Program and Implementation Guide** **69**


**Spelling Assessments**
Spelling assessments are provided for Grades 1–5. They are embedded within the units. Spelling
analysis sheets are provided in Teacher Guides to support teachers in assessing student progress
across the spelling patterns taught.

##### **Writing Assessments**


The writing assessment directly aligns with the knowledge-building of the unit. Students learn
explicit writing skills across the unit and respond to a writing prompt that aligns to the content/
topic of the unit. Writing rubrics are provided in Teacher Guides to support teachers in assessing
student progress across the writing genre.

##### **STAAR-Aligned Question Types**


In Grades 3–5, STAAR-aligned questions are embedded into the instructional materials. Students
will also have an opportunity to engage in STAAR-aligned writing tasks, as well as interact with
writing rubrics that provide clear guidance for achieving end-of-year expectations. These can be
found within the following locations:


- the comprehension questions

- the Guided Reading supports

- the Exit Tickets

- part of the activity page

- in some print and digital end-of-unit assessments


These question types can include hot text, multipart, multiple select, inline choice, short
constructed response, and extended constructed response.


For more information on the STAAR question types, visit the Texas Education Agency website.


**70** **Program and Implementation Guide** **Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts**

**72** **Program and Implementation Guide** **Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts**


### QTI Assessment Guidance

Question & Test Interoperability Assessments, or QTI Assessments, are digitally implemented
in Grades K–5 to measure students’ independent application of literacy skills. In Grades K–2,
assessments are designed to evaluate listening comprehension and vocabulary through audiobased passages and items. In Grades 3–5, reading comprehension, vocabulary, grammar, and
morphology are assessed through independent reading of passages and related questions.


Across grade levels, reading passages include the knowledge and associated vocabulary in
the units taught to students. Each assessment item has an objective that is designed to gauge
students’ mastery of the TEKS, with items that reflect a range of Depth of Knowledge (DOK) levels.
The assessments increase in complexity and length to mirror knowledge building as students
progress through instruction. End-of-unit (EOU) assessments are administered at the end of each
unit to help teacher analyze data and respond to students’ needs. There are digital assessments
for all units except the K-5 research units and the novel study units in Grades 4 and 5, as these units
are not pedagogically aligned to the framework of the QTI assessments.


QTI files can only be viewed and administered once they have been ingested into a Learning
Management System. It is recommended that administrators select either the print or QTI
Assessment method for students. Students should not take both assessment types at the end of a
unit.


Guidelines for accommodating QTI Assessments for students may include but are not limited to
reducing the number of questions, providing breaks, taking a portion of the test and completing the
remaining items later, or any other accommodation that align to a student’s IEP, 504, and/or other
accommodation plan.

##### **Administration**


QTI assessments have an approximate administration time frame of 45–50 minutes, or an
individual class period. During the test administration, teachers and administrators can expect the
following QTI Assessment components by grade band.


**Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts** **Program and Implementation Guide** **73**


**Grades K–2:**
Students are administered an audio-based reading passage, based on the knowledge in the
unit, that they are hearing for the first time.
Images related to the passage are visible for students as they listen.
Students answer questions that are read aloud.
Questions include multiple choice.


**Grades 3–5:**
Students independently read a passage, based on the knowledge in the unit, that they are
reading for the first time.
Students read and answer questions independently.
Questions include multiple choice and other STAAR-aligned item types.
##### **Descriptions of Items**


**Multiple Choice**
The student will choose the correct answer from a set of possible answer choices.

**Multiple Select**
The student will choose the correct answer(s) from a set of possible answer choices.


**Short Constructed Response**
Reading: The student will give a brief explanation in their own words to demonstrate understanding.
Writing: The student will demonstrate proficiency in the skill by constructing a sentence that
corrects a revising or editing error.


**Extended Constructed Response**
The student will write an in-depth response by explaining, analyzing, and evaluating information
provided in a reading selection or stimulus.


**Hot Text**
The student selects highlighted text in a sentence, paragraph, or selection.


**74** **Program and Implementation Guide** **Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts**


**Inline Choice**
The student selects the correct answer from a drop-down menu.


**Multipart**
The student responds to a two-part question where Part A and B are scored separately. Part B asks
students to choose the answer that provides text evidence for the answer in Part A.

##### **Item Scoring**


The items on QTI Assessments have one of the following scoring systems assigned, based on the
question type.


**1.** **Exact Match:** The item has only one correct answer option; for example, a multiple-choice
question, an inline-choice question, or a hot text with only one correct option. The student
receives the full credit of 1 point for each correct exact match question.


**2.** **Partial Match per Response:** The item requires multiple answers to be chosen correctly for the
student to receive the full credit of 1 point. For example, in a multiple-select item with two correct
answers for the full credit of 1 point, a student earns 0.5 points for each correct answer.


**3.** **Written Response:** Short constructed responses—reading are scored on a 2-point rubric, and
extended constructed responses are scored on a 10-point rubric. Short constructed responses—
revising and editing are worth 1 point.


Data results for teacher and administrator reports are contingent upon the platform used by the
district or school to administer the QTI Assessments. QTI Assessment Guides are provided with the
unit materials. Teachers can print the guides or view them online to see the assessment passages,
items, and answer keys. These can be analyzed during the unit internalization process referenced in
the Program Implementation Guidance section.


**Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts** **Program and Implementation Guide** **75**


### Program Implementation Guidance

For a comprehensive understanding of the instructional materials provided by the Bluebonnet
Learning [TM] K–5 Reading Language Arts Program, professional development resources for teachers,
coaches, and administrators are provided.


These materials include internalization protocols that support educators using the program in
effectively implementing and using the high-quality instructional materials (HQIM) provided.


Internalization is the process of deeply studying a unit or lesson from your HQIM to understand
what students are expected to learn and how you will teach it to achieve those outcomes. The
internalization of HQIM is different from traditional “planning” and enables teachers to utilize
their expertise and creativity more effectively to engage and differentiate for all students. HQIM
internalization helps to ensure that all students get access to rigorous and engaging grade-level
content. It also improves the quality of differentiation and in-the-moment support that students
receive. The goal of internalization is to provide equitable instruction and student success. Because
it is critical for teachers to learn and internalize their HQIM effectively, the Texas Educational
Agency has provided the following materials to support all administrators, teachers, and coaches
in facilitating meaningful learning experiences with the grade-level content provided within the
Bluebonnet Learning [TM] K–5 Reading Language Arts Program.


This includes unit-level internalization where teachers and coaches engage in a step-by-step
process for understanding each unit prior to teaching, including what students will be learning, how
students will be assessed, and the high-level arc of learning. By starting with unit internalization,
teachers see how each lesson fits into the big picture prior to using the Lesson Internalization
Protocol.


Unit-level internalization documents:

    - K–2 Reading Language Arts Unit Internalization for Teachers

    - K–3 Foundational Skills Unit Internalization for Teachers

    - 3–5 Unit Internalization for Teachers

    - K–2 Reading Language Arts Unit Internalization for Coaches

    - K–3 Foundational Skills Unit Internalization for Coaches

    - 3–5 Unit Internalization for Coaches


**76** **Program and Implementation Guide** **Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts**


**Bluebonnet Learning K–5 Reading Language Arts** **Program and Implementation Guide** **77**


Following the unit internalization, teachers will engage in the lesson internalization. The Lesson
Internalization Protocol is the process by which teachers understand what students will learn
in a specific lesson, how students will be assessed, and how teachers will make decisions about
how to teach the lesson and support all students to be successful. The Lesson Internalization
Protocol builds on the understanding of the overall unit developed as part of the Unit Internalization
Protocol.


Lesson-level internalization documents:

    - K–2 Reading Language Arts Unit Internalization for Teachers

    - K–3 Foundational Skills Unit Internalization for Teachers

    - 3–5 Unit Internalization for Teachers

    - K–2 Reading Language Arts Unit Internalization for Coaches

    - K–3 Foundational Skills Unit Internalization for Coaches

    - 3–5 Unit Internalization for Coaches

In addition to these resources, is the
Observation Tool. The Observation
tool is a resource for coaches and/or

look-fors while observing teachers’
instruction and implementation of highquality instructional materials. This is not
an evaluative tool, but rather a support
for coaches and/or administrators to
collect observable data. Coaches and/or
administrators can use the data collected
to develop individualized coaching plans
for teachers or grade-level teams. The
data may also be used to develop campuswide or district-wide professional learning
sessions as needed.
